III
à®à®®à¯à®®à¯à®ªà¯ à®ªà¯à®²à®à¯ à®à®µà®¿à®à®°à¯à®®à¯ à®à®³à®°à¯? à®à®©à®à¯ à®à®¿à®²à®°à¯. à®à®´à¯à®¤à®ªà¯ à®ªà¯à®±à®ªà¯à®ªà®à¯à®®à¯à®ªà¯à®¤à¯ à®à¯à®à¯à®à®¿à®±à®¾à®°à¯à®à®³à¯. à®à®µà®°à¯à®à®³à¯ à®à¯à®³à¯à®µà®¿à®¯à®¿à®²à¯ à®à®£à¯à®®à¯à®¯à¯à®®à¯ à®à®°à¯à®à¯à®à®¿à®±à®¤à¯.

à®ªà®´à®à¯à®à®¾à®²à®à¯ à®à®µà®¿à®à®°à¯à®à®³à¯à®¯à¯à®²à¯à®²à®¾à®®à¯ à®à®´à®¿à®¤à¯à®¤à¯à®ªà¯ à®ªà¯à®à®¿ à®µà®¿à®à¯à®µ à®¤à®¾à®²à¯à®®à¯, à®¤à®®à¯ à®à®¾à®²à®à¯ à®à®µà®¿à®à®°à¯à®à®³à¯à®¯à¯à®²à¯à®²à®¾à®®à¯ à®ªà®´à®¿à®¤à¯à®¤à¯ à®¨à®à¯à®¤à¯à®¤à¯ à®µà®¿à®à¯à®µà®¤à®¾à®²à¯à®®à¯ à®¤à®¾à®®à¯ à®®à®à¯à®à¯à®®à¯ à®à®µà®¿à®à®°à®¾à®à®¿ à®µà®¿à®à¯à®µà®¤à®¾à®à®à¯ à®à®¿à®²à®°à¯ à®¨à®¿à®©à¯à®ªà¯à®ªà¯. à®à®µà®°à¯à®à®³à¯ à®à®µà®¿à®à®°à¯à®à®³à¯ à®à®²à¯à®²à®°à¯; à®¤à®¾à®®à¯ à®à®®à®°à¯à®¨à¯à®¤à®¿à®°à¯à®à¯à®à¯à®®à¯ `à®à¯à®à¯ à®à¯à®±à¯à®à¯à®à¯à®®à¯ à®à®±à®¿à®à®°à¯à®à®³à¯. à®ªà®´à¯à®¯ à®à®²à®à¯à®à®¿à®¯à®à¯à®à®³à®¿à®©à¯ à®à®®à¯à®ªà¯à®ªà¯, à®ªà¯à®à¯à®à¯, à®¨à®à¯ à®®à¯à®¤à®²à®¿à®¯ à®à®¿à®±à®ªà¯à®ªà¯à®à¯à®à®³à¯ à®à®µà®°à¯à®à®³à¯ à®¤à®¿à®°à¯à®®à¯à®ªà®¿à®¯à¯à®®à¯ à®ªà®¾à®°à¯à®ªà¯à®ªà®¤à®¿à®²à¯à®²à¯. à®à®¤à®©à®¾à®²à¯ à®à®µà®°à¯à®à®à¯à®à¯à®ªà¯ à®ªà®°à®®à¯à®ªà®°à¯ à®à®£à®°à¯à®µà¯à®®à¯ à®µà®¾à®¯à¯à®ªà¯à®ªà®¤à®¿à®²à¯à®²à¯.

IV

An appreciation
by
VR. M. CHETTIAR, B.A.,
`Mudiarasanâ is a modern Tamil poet who is young, enthusiastic and sings with gusto of lifeâs perplexing problems: he is a born poet, a genius indeed who enjoys life, finds out the poignant secrets of
existence, and rapturously exercises his ardent imagination in
building up his human theme, without being baffled by the occasional riddles of social evils and human deviations and distractions.
When he sings of Natureâs myriad graces, he is enthralled by the beauty of creation which has a perennia sweetness and consoling solemnity, as a wholesome remedy for the human camouflage and delinquency of conduct.
When he sings of love, the human secrets of sweeter existence emerge in a transparent poetic picture which sincerely thrills the reader who easily understands and enjoys the poetâs solemn secrets
profoundly and sensitively.
When he deals with the relation between capital and labour, he goes to the root of the trouble..... the uneven distribution of wealth, the tyrannical capitalist and the struggling labourer who perhaps under a benign rule can enjoy life better, tenderly and tranquilly.
When the poet discusses the importance of Tamil as our mother-tongue, his rapture knows no bounds: he is frank, ecstatic, and
assuring in his profound poetic utterance, insisting on the sincerity of his over helming suggestions. Even child can easily grasp the
fundamental brilliance of his argument in defence of his mother-tongue with all its alluring charms of sweeter delicacy and expansive 
accommodation.
When Mudiarasan recalls to his memory the achievements of Bharathithasan, Kalianasundara Mudaliar, Desika Vinayagam Pillai and the Crucifixion of Jesus Christ, he cheerfully details their solemn and enduring merits which the world always welcomes as a universal
triumph of the human spirit summoned by the human crises.
When his poems tranquilly bless the souls of the great departed Indians, they have the geunine tenderness of a warm, holy enduring benediction indeed.
His miscellaneous poems enlighten us on the poetic profundity of Kambarâs genius in its entire universa appeal of artistic
resplendency.
Mudiarasanâs poetry is charming indeed both in matter and manner: his prosodic variety will please all, and his poetic diction is racy, vivid, ripping, subtle, resonant and suggestive, employing his own concrete, convincing imagery to vivify the imaginative spell of happy human experiences in lifeâs heaving cosmos.
The poetâs ethical emphasis is direct, and never deviates from the central crisis of lifeâs languorous lavishness.
We may assure the young poet a glorious future in the world of growing modern Tamil poetry in its expansive accommodative march. His poems console us tenderly, peacefully and permanently.
His musical compositions appear as a separate book of varied graces and inspiration: the exhilarated reader can welcome therein the poetâs dignity, and clarity of harmonious diction designed for the ecstasy of musical utterance. Simple words sing rapturously, inducing a fountain of delight in the listenerâs ear.
Karaikudi,	VR.M. CHETTIAR
11-3-1961
